# 🚀 Step 1 — Investigation Engine

Create this folder:

```
app/
 └── investigation/
```

Inside it create:

```
intent_classifier.py
dispatcher.py
```

---

## intent_classifier.py

```python
def classify(question: str):

    q = question.lower()

    if any(word in q for word in [
        "repeat offender",
        "habitual",
        "repeat criminal"
    ]):
        return "repeat_offenders"

    if any(word in q for word in [
        "trend",
        "statistics",
        "crime trend"
    ]):
        return "crime_trends"

    if any(word in q for word in [
        "network",
        "associate",
        "gang",
        "relationship"
    ]):
        return "criminal_network"

    if any(word in q for word in [
        "hotspot",
        "district",
        "location"
    ]):
        return "hotspots"

    return "sql"
```

---

## dispatcher.py

```python
from app.investigation.intent_classifier import classify

from app.analytics.repeat_offenders import repeat_offenders
from app.analytics.crime_trends import crime_trends
from app.analytics.criminal_network import criminal_network
from app.analytics.hotspots import crime_hotspots

def dispatch(question, db):

    intent = classify(question)

    if intent == "repeat_offenders":
        return repeat_offenders(db)

    if intent == "crime_trends":
        return crime_trends(db)

    if intent == "criminal_network":
        return criminal_network(db)

    if intent == "hotspots":
        return crime_hotspots(db)

    return None
```

---

# Step 2 — Modify AI Service

Your AI service should follow this flow:

```text
User Question
      │
      ▼
Dispatcher
      │
      ├── Analytics Match?
      │        │
      │        ▼
      │   Return Analytics Result
      │
      ▼
Gemini SQL Generator
      │
      ▼
Execute SQL
      │
      ▼
Gemini Explanation
```

Pseudo-code:

```python
analytics = dispatch(question, db)

if analytics is not None:
    return {
        "source": "analytics",
        "data": analytics
    }

# Otherwise continue with Gemini SQL
```

---

# 🚀 Step 3 — Standard Response Format

Every endpoint (analytics or AI) should return the same structure:

```json
{
  "success": true,
  "source": "analytics",
  "intent": "crime_trends",
  "question": "Show crime trends",
  "rows_returned": 5,
  "data": [
    ...
  ],
  "explanation": "..."
}
```

This makes it easy for the React frontend to consume any response.

---

```
app/utils/logger.py
```

```python
import logging

logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s %(levelname)s %(message)s"
)

logger = logging.getLogger("ksp")
```

Log every investigation:

```python
logger.info(f"Question: {question}")
logger.info(f"Intent: {intent}")
```

This is useful for debugging during the hackathon.

### Most likely causes

### ✅ Case 1: React project wasn't created

If `package.json` doesn't contain something like:

```json
"scripts": {
  "dev": "vite",
  "build": "vite build",
  "preview": "vite preview"
}
```

then the React app was never initialized.

Create it with:

```bash
cd H:\KPS-Crime-AI
npm create vite@latest frontend -- --template react
cd frontend
npm install
npm run dev
```

---

### ✅ Case 2: Wrong folder

If you're inside a folder that only contains `node_modules` or a different `package.json`, `npm run dev` won't exist.

## Response:
09/07/2026, 00:29:52

I found the problem. 👍

Your `package.json` is **not a React project**. It only contains dependencies—you never created the Vite app, so there are no scripts like `dev`, `build`, or `preview`.

Your current `package.json`:

```json
{
  "dependencies": {
    ...
  }
}
```

A Vite React project should look something like:

```json
{
  "name": "frontend",
  "private": true,
  "version": "0.0.0",
  "type": "module",
  "scripts": {
    "dev": "vite",
    "build": "vite build",
    "preview": "vite preview"
  },
  "dependencies": {
    "react": "...",
    "react-dom": "..."
  },
  "devDependencies": {
    "vite": "...",
    "@vitejs/plugin-react": "..."
  }
}
```

## The easiest fix (5 minutes)

Delete the incomplete frontend and recreate it properly.

### 1. Go to the project root

```bash
cd H:\KPS-Crime-AI
```

### 2. Delete the broken frontend

PowerShell:

```powershell
Remove-Item -Recurse -Force frontend
```

or simply delete the `frontend` folder from File Explorer.

### 3. Create a proper React app

```bash
npm create vite@latest frontend -- --template react
```

Choose the defaults if prompted.

### 4. Enter the folder

```bash
cd frontend
```

### 5. Install everything

```bash
npm install
```

### 6. Start React

```bash
npm run dev
```

You should see something like:

```text
VITE v...

```

### 7. Then install our extra packages

```bash
npm install axios react-router-dom recharts reactflow react-icons react-leaflet leaflet jspdf html2canvas react-speech-recognition
```


# 🚀 Step 4: Create API Service

Create:

`src/services/api.js`

```javascript
import axios from "axios";

const api = axios.create({
    baseURL: "http://127.0.0.1:8000",
    headers: {
        "Content-Type": "application/json",
    },
});

export default api;
```

Now every component can simply do:

```javascript
import api from "../services/api";

const response = await api.get("/analytics/crime-trends");
```

# Step 5 — App Routing

Replace `App.jsx` with:

```jsx
import { BrowserRouter, Routes, Route } from "react-router-dom";

import Dashboard from "./pages/Dashboard";
import Cases from "./pages/Cases";
import Analytics from "./pages/Analytics";
import Investigation from "./pages/Investigation";
import Reports from "./pages/Reports";

function App() {
  return (
    <BrowserRouter>
      <Routes>
        <Route path="/" element={<Dashboard />} />
        <Route path="/cases" element={<Cases />} />
        <Route path="/analytics" element={<Analytics />} />
        <Route path="/investigation" element={<Investigation />} />
        <Route path="/reports" element={<Reports />} />
      </Routes>
    </BrowserRouter>
  );
}

export default App;
```

---

# Step 6 — Placeholder Pages

For now, put this in each page (`Dashboard.jsx`, `Cases.jsx`, etc.):

```jsx
export default function Dashboard() {
  return (
    <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold p-10">
      Dashboard
    </h1>
  );
}
```

Change the component name and text for each page.

# Step 1 — Create `Layout.jsx`

📁 `src/components/layout/Layout.jsx`

```jsx
import Sidebar from "./Sidebar";
import Navbar from "./Navbar";

export default function Layout({ children }) {
  return (
    <div className="flex h-screen bg-slate-100">
      <Sidebar />

      <div className="flex-1 flex flex-col">
        <Navbar />

        <main className="flex-1 p-6 overflow-auto">
          {children}
        </main>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

---

# Step 2 — Create `Sidebar.jsx`

📁 `src/components/layout/Sidebar.jsx`

```jsx
import { Link } from "react-router-dom";
import {
  FaHome,
  FaFolderOpen,
  FaChartBar,
  FaProjectDiagram,
  FaFileAlt,
  FaCog,
} from "react-icons/fa";

export default function Sidebar() {
  const menu = [
    { name: "Dashboard", icon: <FaHome />, path: "/" },
    { name: "Cases", icon: <FaFolderOpen />, path: "/cases" },
    { name: "Analytics", icon: <FaChartBar />, path: "/analytics" },
    { name: "Investigation", icon: <FaProjectDiagram />, path: "/investigation" },
    { name: "Reports", icon: <FaFileAlt />, path: "/reports" },
  ];

  return (
    <div className="w-64 bg-slate-900 text-white flex flex-col">
      <div className="text-2xl font-bold p-6 border-b border-slate-700">
        🚔 KSP AI
      </div>

      <nav className="flex-1">
        {menu.map((item) => (
          <Link
            key={item.name}
            to={item.path}
            className="flex items-center gap-3 px-6 py-4 hover:bg-slate-800 transition"
          >
            {item.icon}
            {item.name}
          </Link>
        ))}
      </nav>

      <div className="p-6 border-t border-slate-700 flex items-center gap-3">
        <FaCog />
        Settings
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

---

## Response:
09/07/2026, 01:01:47

I found the problem immediately. 🎯

You **installed Tailwind**, but you **didn't configure it**.

Your `vite.config.js` is missing the Tailwind plugin, and your `index.css` is still the default Vite stylesheet.

---

# ✅ Fix 1: Update `vite.config.js`

Replace it with:

```javascript
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import react from "@vitejs/plugin-react";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    react(),
    tailwindcss(),
  ],
});
```

---

# ✅ Fix 2: Install the Tailwind Vite plugin

From the `frontend` folder, run:

```bash
npm install tailwindcss @tailwindcss/vite
```

---

# ✅ Fix 3: Replace `src/index.css`

Delete **everything** inside `src/index.css`.

Replace it with exactly this:

```css
@import "tailwindcss";

html,
body,
#root {
  margin: 0;
  padding: 0;
  width: 100%;
  min-height: 100vh;
}

body {
  background: #f1f5f9;
  font-family: Inter, Arial, sans-serif;
}
```

The long CSS you pasted is the default Vite template. We don't need it.

---

# ✅ Fix 4: Restart Vite

```bash
Ctrl + C
npm run dev
```

start

## Response:
09/07/2026, 01:04:48

Perfect. 🚀 Let's build the first **live dashboard** by connecting React to your FastAPI backend.

---

# Step 1 — Create a Dashboard Statistics API

First, let's make one backend endpoint that returns all dashboard statistics in a single call.

## 📄 `app/api/dashboard.py`

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter
from sqlalchemy import text
from app.database.connection import engine

router = APIRouter(
    prefix="/dashboard",
    tags=["Dashboard"]
)

@router.get("/stats")
def dashboard_stats():

    with engine.connect() as conn:

        total_cases = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM casemaster")
        ).scalar()

        total_criminals = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM accuseddetails")
        ).scalar()

        total_complainants = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM complainantdetails")
        ).scalar()

        return {
            "total_cases": total_cases,
            "total_criminals": total_criminals,
            "total_complainants": total_complainants,
            "active_cases": total_cases
        }
```

---

## Register the router

In `main.py`

```python
from app.api import dashboard
```

and

```python
app.include_router(dashboard.router)
```

Restart FastAPI.

Test:

```
http://127.0.0.1:8000/dashboard/stats
```

Expected:

```json
{
  "total_cases": 142,
  "total_criminals": 95,
  "total_complainants": 110,
  "active_cases": 142
}
```

# Step 2 — Create StatsCard Component

📁 `src/components/dashboard/StatsCard.jsx`

```jsx
export default function StatsCard({ title, value, icon }) {
  return (
    <div className="bg-white rounded-xl shadow-md p-6 hover:shadow-lg transition">
      <div className="text-4xl mb-3">{icon}</div>

      <div className="text-gray-500">
        {title}
      </div>

      <div className="text-3xl font-bold mt-2">
        {value}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

---

# Step 3 — Update Dashboard Page

Replace `Dashboard.jsx`

```jsx
import { useEffect, useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/layout/Layout";
import StatsCard from "../components/dashboard/StatsCard";
import api from "../services/api";

export default function Dashboard() {

  const [stats, setStats] = useState({
    total_cases: 0,
    total_criminals: 0,
    total_complainants: 0,
    active_cases: 0,
  });

  useEffect(() => {
    api.get("/dashboard/stats")
      .then((res) => setStats(res.data))
      .catch(console.error);
  }, []);

  return (
    <Layout>

      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-8">
        Dashboard
      </h1>

      <div className="grid grid-cols-4 gap-6">

        <StatsCard
          title="Total Cases"
          value={stats.total_cases}
          icon="📂"
        />

        <StatsCard
          title="Criminals"
          value={stats.total_criminals}
          icon="👤"
        />

        <StatsCard
          title="Complainants"
          value={stats.total_complainants}
          icon="🙋"
        />

        <StatsCard
          title="Active Cases"
          value={stats.active_cases}
          icon="🚔"
        />

      </div>

    </Layout>
  );
}
```

## Response:
09/07/2026, 01:07:58

This is actually **good news**. 🎉 Your React dashboard is successfully calling the backend. The only problem is that the SQL query is pointing to a table that doesn't exist.

The error is:

```text
relation "accuseddetails" does not exist
```

This means your PostgreSQL database does **not** have a table named `accuseddetails`.

## Step 1: Find the correct table name

Open **pgAdmin** or **psql** and run:

```sql
SELECT tablename
FROM pg_tables
WHERE schemaname = 'public';
```

or in psql:

```sql
\dt
```

Paste the output here.

---

## Step 2: Update the dashboard query

If your table is named `accused` instead of `accuseddetails`, change:

```python
text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM accuseddetails")
```

to

```python
text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM accused")
```

Likewise, if the complainant table has a different name, update:

```python
text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM complainantdetails")
```

to the correct table name.

---

## Temporary solution (to keep the dashboard working)

If those tables aren't created yet, modify `dashboard.py` to only use existing tables:

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter
from sqlalchemy import text
from app.database.connection import engine

router = APIRouter(prefix="/dashboard", tags=["Dashboard"])

@router.get("/stats")
def dashboard_stats():
    with engine.connect() as conn:
        total_cases = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM casemaster")
        ).scalar()

    return {
        "total_cases": total_cases,
        "total_criminals": 0,
        "total_complainants": 0,
        "active_cases": total_cases,
    }
```

This will let your React dashboard display live data immediately while we finish the remaining tables.

# While we're here, let's make the dashboard much better 🚀

Instead of just 4 basic cards, let's create a **Police Command Dashboard**.

## Replace your dashboard response with:

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter
from sqlalchemy import text
from app.database.connection import engine

router = APIRouter(prefix="/dashboard", tags=["Dashboard"])

@router.get("/stats")
def dashboard_stats():

    with engine.connect() as conn:

        total_cases = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM casemaster")
        ).scalar()

        total_criminals = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM accused")
        ).scalar()

        total_complainants = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM complainantdetails")
        ).scalar()

        total_vehicles = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM vehicle")
        ).scalar()

        total_evidence = conn.execute(
            text("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM evidence")
        ).scalar()

        return {
            "total_cases": total_cases,
            "criminals": total_criminals,
            "complainants": total_complainants,
            "vehicles": total_vehicles,
            "evidence": total_evidence
        }
```

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:26:19

😂 I know exactly what happened.

You accidentally pasted **Python FastAPI code into your React file**.

The error says:

```text
src/pages/Dashboard.jsx

from fastapi import APIRouter
```

`Dashboard.jsx` is a **React (JavaScript/JSX)** file, so it cannot contain Python code.

---

## Fix it

### 1. Open:

```
frontend/src/pages/Dashboard.jsx
```

Delete everything.

Paste this React code:

```jsx
import { useEffect, useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/layout/Layout";
import StatsCard from "../components/dashboard/StatsCard";
import api from "../services/api";

export default function Dashboard() {
  const [stats, setStats] = useState({
    total_cases: 0,
    criminals: 0,
    complainants: 0,
    vehicles: 0,
    evidence: 0,
  });

  useEffect(() => {
    api.get("/dashboard/stats")
      .then((res) => setStats(res.data))
      .catch(console.error);
  }, []);

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-6">Dashboard</h1>

      <div className="grid grid-cols-5 gap-5">
        <StatsCard title="Cases" value={stats.total_cases} icon="📂" />
        <StatsCard title="Criminals" value={stats.criminals} icon="👤" />
        <StatsCard title="Complainants" value={stats.complainants} icon="👥" />
        <StatsCard title="Vehicles" value={stats.vehicles} icon="🚗" />
        <StatsCard title="Evidence" value={stats.evidence} icon="📄" />
      </div>
    </Layout>
  );
}
```

---

### 2. Put the Python code here instead:

```
backend/app/api/dashboard.py
```

The code that starts with:

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter
```

belongs **only** in the backend.

---

## Project separation

```
KPS-Crime-AI/
│
├── backend/        ← Python (FastAPI)
│      app/
│      api/
│      models/
│
└── frontend/       ← React
       src/
       pages/
       components/
```

- 🐍 **Backend** = Python (`from fastapi import ...`)
- ⚛️ **Frontend** = React (`import React from ...`)

Never mix the two.

---

### After fixing it

Restart both:

**Backend**

```bash
uvicorn app.main:app --reload
```

**Frontend**

```bash
npm run dev
```

---

## From now on, I'll clearly label every code block with where it belongs:

- 🐍 **BACKEND:** `backend/app/...`
- ⚛️ **FRONTEND:** `frontend/src/...`

This will help avoid accidentally placing backend code into frontend files as we continue building the platform.

# Step 1 — Create the API service

📁 **Frontend**
```
frontend/src/services/api.js
```

Install Axios if you haven't already:

```bash
npm install axios
```

Then create `api.js`:

```javascript
import axios from "axios";

const api = axios.create({
  baseURL: "http://127.0.0.1:8000",
});

export default api;
```

---

# Step 2 — Create the AI Investigation page

📁 **Frontend**
```
frontend/src/pages/Investigation.jsx
```

Paste:

```jsx
import { useState } from "react";
import api from "../services/api";

export default function Investigation() {

  const [question, setQuestion] = useState("");
  const [response, setResponse] = useState(null);
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  const askAI = async () => {
    if (!question) return;

    setLoading(true);

    try {
      const res = await api.post("/ai/query", {
        question: question
      });

      setResponse(res.data);

    } catch (err) {
      console.log(err);
      alert("Backend Error");
    }

    setLoading(false);
  };

  return (
    <div style={{padding:"30px"}}>

      <h1>🤖 AI Investigation Assistant</h1>

      <input
        style={{
          width:"70%",
          padding:"12px",
          fontSize:"16px"
        }}
        placeholder="Ask anything..."
        value={question}
        onChange={(e)=>setQuestion(e.target.value)}
      />

      <button
        onClick={askAI}
        style={{
          marginLeft:"15px",
          padding:"12px 25px"
        }}
      >
        Ask AI
      </button>

      {loading && <h3>Thinking...</h3>}

      {response && (

        <div style={{marginTop:"30px"}}>

          <h2>Generated SQL</h2>

          <pre>{response.generated_sql}</pre>

          <h2>Rows Returned</h2>

          <pre>{response.rows_returned}</pre>

          <h2>Data</h2>

          <pre>
            {JSON.stringify(response.data,null,2)}
          </pre>

          <h2>AI Explanation</h2>

          <p>{response.explanation}</p>

        </div>

      )}

    </div>
  );
}
```

---

with:

```javascript
catch (err) {
  console.error(err);

  if (err.response) {
    console.log(err.response.data);
    alert(JSON.stringify(err.response.data, null, 2));
  } else {
    alert(err.message);
  }
```

## Most likely causes

- ❌ `POST /ai/query` route doesn't exist (404)
- ❌ Request body doesn't match the Pydantic model (422)

- ❌ AI service can't connect to the database (500)

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:35:21

Excellent—this isn't a bug in your code. 🎉

The important part is:

```text
google.genai.errors.ServerError: 503 UNAVAILABLE

This model is currently experiencing high demand.
Please try again later.
```

Your:
- ✅ Frontend is working.
- ✅ FastAPI endpoint is working.
- ✅ Database connection is working.
- ✅ Gemini API key is valid.

The failure is on **Google's Gemini server**, which is temporarily overloaded.

---

# Fix 1 (Recommended): Retry Automatically

Open:

```text
backend/app/ai/gemini_client.py
```

Wrap the call in a retry loop:

```python
import time
from google import genai

client = genai.Client(api_key="YOUR_API_KEY")

def ask_gemini(prompt):
    for attempt in range(3):
        try:
            response = client.models.generate_content(
                model="gemini-2.5-flash",
                contents=prompt,
            )
            return response.text

        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Retry {attempt+1}: {e}")
            time.sleep(2)

    raise Exception("Gemini service unavailable.")
```

---

# Fix 2 (Even Better): Graceful Fallback

In:

```text
backend/app/services/ai_service.py
```

Change:

```python
sql = generate_sql(question)
```

to:

```python
try:
    sql = generate_sql(question)
except Exception:
    return {
        "success": False,
        "message": "Gemini is temporarily busy. Please try again in a few seconds."
    }
```

Now your app won't crash with a 500 error—it will return a friendly JSON response.

---

# Fix 3 (Best for Hackathon): Use a Faster Model

If you're using:

```python
model="gemini-2.5-flash"
```

try switching to:

```python
model="gemini-2.0-flash"
```

or, if your SDK supports it:

```python
model="gemini-2.0-flash-lite"
```

These models are often less congested and respond faster.

---

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:38:05

That error is because the `try/except` block is incomplete or incorrectly indented.

The traceback points to:

```text
backend/app/services/ai_service.py
line 11

SyntaxError: expected 'except' or 'finally' block
```

This usually happens when the code looks like:

```python
def process_query(question):
    try:
        sql = generate_sql(question)

    return {
        ...
    }

except Exception:
    ...
```

or the `except` is not aligned with the `try`.

## Replace your entire `process_query()` function with this:

```python
from app.ai.sql_generator import generate_sql
from app.ai.query_executor import execute_sql
from app.ai.explainer import explain_results

def process_query(question):
    try:
        sql = generate_sql(question)

        rows = execute_sql(sql)

        explanation = explain_results(question, rows)

        return {
            "success": True,
            "question": question,
            "generated_sql": sql,
            "rows_returned": len(rows),
            "data": rows,
            "explanation": explanation
        }

    except Exception as e:
        return {
            "success": False,
            "error": str(e)
        }
```

Notice that:

- `try:` and `except:` are at the **same indentation level**.
- Everything inside `try:` is indented by 4 spaces.

## Let's create them.

### 📁 Create: `backend/app/ai/query_executor.py`

```python
from sqlalchemy import text
from app.database.connection import engine

def execute_sql(sql: str):
    with engine.connect() as conn:
        result = conn.execute(text(sql))

        try:
            return [dict(row._mapping) for row in result]
        except Exception:
            return []
```

---

### 📁 Create: `backend/app/ai/explainer.py`

```python
from app.ai.gemini_client import ask_gemini

def explain_results(question, rows):
    prompt = f"""
You are a police investigation assistant.

Question:
{question}

Results:
{rows}

Explain the results in simple English for an investigating officer.
"""

    try:
        return ask_gemini(prompt)
    except Exception:
        return "AI explanation is temporarily unavailable."
```

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:43:09

I found the problem immediately. 🎯

Your code has:

```python
client = genai.Client(api_key="YOUR_API_KEY")
```

That is literally using the text `"YOUR_API_KEY"` instead of your actual Gemini API key.

## Fix it properly

### 1. Install python-dotenv

```bash
pip install python-dotenv
```

---

### 2. Create `.env`

In your **backend** folder:

```
backend/
│
├── .env
├── app/
├── venv/
```

Contents:

```env
GEMINI_API_KEY=AIzaSyXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
```

### 3. Replace `gemini_client.py`

```python
import os
import time

from dotenv import load_dotenv
from google import genai

load_dotenv()

API_KEY = os.getenv("GEMINI_API_KEY")

if not API_KEY:
    raise Exception("GEMINI_API_KEY not found in .env")

client = genai.Client(api_key=API_KEY)

def ask_gemini(prompt):
    for attempt in range(3):
        try:
            response = client.models.generate_content(
                model="gemini-2.5-flash",
                contents=prompt
            )

            return response.text

        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Attempt {attempt+1}: {e}")
            time.sleep(2)

    raise Exception("Gemini service unavailable.")
```

```
├── Accused
├── Criminal History

├── Vehicles

└── Investigation Officer
```

```json
{

  "complainant": {...},
  "victim": {...},
  "accused": [...],
  "criminal_history": [...],
  "vehicles": [...],
```

# Architecture

```
Frontend
    │
    ▼
GET /investigation/{case_id}
    │
    ▼
FastAPI
    │
    ▼
Investigation Service
    │
    ├── Case
    ├── Complainant
    ├── Victim
    ├── Accused
    ├── Criminal History
    ├── Known Associates
    ├── Vehicles
    ├── Evidence
    └── Investigation Officer
```

---

# STEP 1

## Create

```
backend/app/api/investigation.py
```

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter
from sqlalchemy import text

from app.database.connection import engine

router = APIRouter(prefix="/investigation", tags=["Investigation"])

@router.get("/{case_id}")
def investigation(case_id: int):

    with engine.connect() as conn:

        case = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM casemaster
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().first()

        complainant = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM complainantdetails
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

        victim = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM victim
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

        accused = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM accused
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

        evidence = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM evidence
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

        vehicles = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM vehicle
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

        officer = conn.execute(text("""
            SELECT *
            FROM investigationofficer
            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().first()

    return {
        "case": case,
        "complainants": complainant,
        "victims": victim,
        "accused": accused,
        "vehicles": vehicles,
        "evidence": evidence,
        "investigation_officer": officer
    }
```

---

# STEP 2

Open

```
app/main.py
```

Import:

```python
from app.api import investigation
```

Register:

```python
app.include_router(investigation.router)
```

```
http://127.0.0.1:8000/docs

```

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:49:04

This is actually good news. 👍 Your API is working, but our assumption about the database schema is wrong.

The error:

```text
column "case_id" does not exist

FROM vehicle
WHERE case_id=2
```

means your **vehicle table does not have a `case_id` column**.

---

## Step 1: Let's inspect the actual schema

Open **pgAdmin** or use your SQL console and run:

```sql
SELECT *
FROM vehicle
LIMIT 1;
```

or

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='vehicle';
```

Paste the output here.

---

## Step 2: Do the same for these tables

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='accused';
```

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='criminalhistory';
```

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='knownassociate';
```

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='evidence';
```

```sql
SELECT column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name='investigationofficer';
```

---

## Why this is happening

I assumed a common police database structure:

```text
vehicle
-------
vehicle_id
case_id   ❌
```

But your Karnataka Police database appears to use a different design, such as:

```text
vehicle
--------
vehicle_id
accused_id
```

or

```text
vehicle
--------
vehicle_id
person_id
```

or another foreign key entirely.

---

## Fastest way forward 🚀

Run this one SQL query to get **every table and its columns**:

```sql
SELECT
    table_name,
    column_name
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_schema = 'public'
ORDER BY table_name, ordinal_position;
```

Copy the result (or export it as CSV) and paste it here.

Once I have the real schema, I'll rewrite the Investigation Engine to match your database exactly—no more guessing. That will save us a lot of debugging time as we build the remaining features.

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:50:39

Perfect! 🎉 This explains the error.

Your schema is actually well designed, but the relationships are different from what we assumed.

The important part is:

```text
vehicle
--------
vehicle_id
person_id      ✅
registration_number
...
```

**There is NO `case_id` in the `vehicle` table.**

Similarly:

```text
knownassociate
---------------
person_id
associate_person_id
```

and

```text
investigationofficer
--------------------
officer_id
name
rank
...
```

Notice that `investigationofficer` also **does not have `case_id`**, so we cannot query it by case.

---

# Fix your `investigation.py`

## ❌ Remove this block

```python
vehicles = conn.execute(text("""
SELECT *
FROM vehicle
WHERE case_id=:id
"""), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()
```

---

## Replace it with

```python
vehicles = []
```

We'll fetch vehicles properly after we connect `personidentity` to accused/complainants.

---

## Remove this too

```python
officer = conn.execute(text("""
SELECT *
FROM investigationofficer
WHERE case_id=:id
"""), {"id": case_id}).mappings().first()
```

Replace with

```python
officer = None
```

---

# Your API should now return

```python
return {
    "case": case,
    "complainants": complainant,
    "victims": victim,
    "accused": accused,
    "vehicles": [],
    "evidence": evidence,
    "investigation_officer": None
}
```

That should eliminate the current SQL errors.

The error is expected based on your schema. 👍

Your `vehicle` table **does not have a `case_id` column**.

From the schema you shared:

```text
vehicle
--------
vehicle_id
person_id
registration_number
vehicle_type
model
color
manufacturer
```

So this code is wrong:

```python
vehicles = conn.execute(text("""
    SELECT *
    FROM vehicle
    WHERE case_id=:id
"""), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()
```

It throws:

```

```

---

## How your database is designed

```
casemaster
   |
   | case_id
   |
accused --------> personidentity
   |                ^
   |                |
   | case_id        | person_id
   |                |
   +----------------+

vehicle
--------
person_id
```

Vehicle belongs to a **person**, not directly to a case.

So you must first find the people involved in a case, then fetch their vehicles.

---

## Correct SQL

For accused vehicles:

```sql
SELECT
    v.*
FROM vehicle v
JOIN accused a
ON v.person_id = a.accused_id
WHERE a.case_id = :id;
```

or if `accused_id` is **not** the same as `person_id`, then your schema is incomplete and you need another mapping table.

---

```
name
gender
age
address
```

```
person_id
```

From your screenshot I can only see

```
name
gender
age
address
```

There is **no `person_id`**.

# I think your schema has a design issue

You currently have

```
vehicle
   person_id
```

but

```
accused

```

No foreign key exists.

The proper design should be

```
personidentity
    person_id

accused
    person_id

victim
    person_id

complainant
    person_id

vehicle
    person_id

phone
    person_id

criminalhistory
    person_id
```

Then everything joins through `person_id`.

def investigation(case_id: int):

            WHERE case_id=:id
        """), {"id": case_id}).mappings().all()

            FROM accused
            WHERE case_id=:id

## Response:
09/07/2026, 11:58:41

Your code is now syntactically correct. ✅

However, I would improve it slightly to make it production-ready and prevent errors when a case doesn't exist.

Replace your file with this:

```python
from fastapi import APIRouter, HTTPException
from sqlalchemy import text

from app.database.connection import engine

router = APIRouter(prefix="/investigation", tags=["Investigation"])

@router.get("/{case_id}")
def investigation(case_id: int):

    with engine.connect() as conn:

        case = conn.execute(
            text("""
                SELECT *
                FROM casemaster
                WHERE case_id=:id
            """),
            {"id": case_id}
        ).mappings().first()

        if not case:
            raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Case not found")

        complainants = conn.execute(
            text("""
                SELECT *
                FROM complainantdetails
                WHERE case_id=:id
            """),
            {"id": case_id}
        ).mappings().all()

        victims = conn.execute(
            text("""
                SELECT *
                FROM victim
                WHERE case_id=:id
            """),
            {"id": case_id}
        ).mappings().all()

        accused = conn.execute(
            text("""
                SELECT *
                FROM accused
                WHERE case_id=:id
            """),
            {"id": case_id}
        ).mappings().all()

        evidence = conn.execute(
            text("""
                SELECT *
                FROM evidence
                WHERE case_id=:id
            """),
            {"id": case_id}
        ).mappings().all()

        # No direct relationship exists between case and vehicle
        vehicles = []

        # Your schema has no case -> officer mapping yet
        investigation_officer = None

    return {
        "success": True,
        "case": case,
        "complainants": complainants,
        "victims": victims,
        "accused": accused,
        "vehicles": vehicles,
        "evidence": evidence,
        "investigation_officer": investigation_officer
    }
```

The error is telling you that the parser reached:

```jsx
catch (err) {
```

but **it never found a matching `try {` block or a closing `}` before it**.

This is almost always caused by one of these:

```jsx
// ❌ Missing try
catch (err) {
```

or

```jsx
try {
   ...
// ❌ Missing closing brace
catch (err) {
```

or

```jsx
useEffect(() => {
    async function load() {
        try {
            ...
        // ❌ Missing }
    catch (err) {
```

## Prompt:

import { useState } from "react";
import api from "../services/api";

export default function Investigation() {

  const [question, setQuestion] = useState("");
  const [response, setResponse] = useState(null);
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  const askAI = async () => {
    if (!question) return;

    setLoading(true);

    try {
      const res = await api.post("/ai/query", {
        question: question
      });

      setResponse(res.data);

    catch (err) {
  console.error(err);

  if (err.response) {
    console.log(err.response.data);
    alert(JSON.stringify(err.response.data, null, 2));
  } else {
    alert(err.message);
  }
}
    setLoading(false);
  };

  return (
    <div style={{padding:"30px"}}>

      <h1>🤖 AI Investigation Assistant</h1>

      <input
        style={{
          width:"70%",
          padding:"12px",
          fontSize:"16px"
        }}
        placeholder="Ask anything..."
        value={question}
        onChange={(e)=>setQuestion(e.target.value)}
      />

      <button
        onClick={askAI}
        style={{
          marginLeft:"15px",
          padding:"12px 25px"
        }}
      >
        Ask AI
      </button>

      {loading && <h3>Thinking...</h3>}

      {response && (

        <div style={{marginTop:"30px"}}>

          <h2>Generated SQL</h2>

          <pre>{response.generated_sql}</pre>

          <h2>Rows Returned</h2>

          <pre>{response.rows_returned}</pre>

          <h2>Data</h2>

          <pre>
            {JSON.stringify(response.data,null,2)}
          </pre>

          <h2>AI Explanation</h2>

          <p>{response.explanation}</p>

        </div>

      )}

    </div>
  );
}

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:04:35

I found the bug immediately. ✅

You're missing the closing brace `}` for the `try` block.

Your code currently has:

```jsx
try {
  const res = await api.post("/ai/query", {
    question: question
  });

  setResponse(res.data);

catch (err) {
```

It should be:

```jsx
try {
  const res = await api.post("/ai/query", {
    question: question
  });

  setResponse(res.data);

} catch (err) {
  console.error(err);

  if (err.response) {
    console.log(err.response.data);
    alert(JSON.stringify(err.response.data, null, 2));
  } else {
    alert(err.message);
  }
} finally {
  setLoading(false);
}
```

So your entire `askAI` function should become:

```jsx
const askAI = async () => {
  if (!question) return;

  setLoading(true);

  try {
    const res = await api.post("/ai/query", {
      question: question,
    });

    setResponse(res.data);

  } catch (err) {
    console.error(err);

    if (err.response) {
      console.log(err.response.data);
      alert(JSON.stringify(err.response.data, null, 2));
    } else {
      alert(err.message);
    }

  } finally {
    setLoading(false);
  }
};
```

### Why this happened

JavaScript syntax is:

```js
try {
   ...
} catch (err) {
   ...
} finally {
   ...
}
```

Your code was missing the `}` before `catch`, so Vite reported:

```
Unexpected token
catch (err)
```

because it was still expecting the end of the `try` block.

After making this change, save the file and Vite should hot reload without the parse error.

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:06:39

The important part is this:

```
OPTIONS /ai/query HTTP/1.1 405 Method Not Allowed
```

This is **not an AI problem**. It's a **CORS problem**.

Your browser sends an **OPTIONS (preflight)** request before the POST request. FastAPI is rejecting it with **405**, so Axios reports **Network Error**.

## Step 1: Check `main.py`

It should look something like this:

```python
from fastapi import FastAPI
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware

from app.api import ai, investigation

app = FastAPI()

app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=[
        "http://localhost:5173",
    ],
    allow_credentials=True,
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"],
)

app.include_router(ai.router)
app.include_router(investigation.router)
```

If `CORSMiddleware` is missing, add it.

## Prompt:
09/07/2026, 12:14:33

🤖 AI Investigation Assistant
show all thrift cases 
Ask AI
Generated SQL
SELECT * FROM casemaster WHERE crime_type = 'Thrift'
Rows Returned
0
Data
[]
AI Explanation
Officer, Based on your request to "show all thrift cases," the system returned: `[]` This means: **There are currently no cases explicitly categorized or tagged as "thrift cases" in our database.** The empty brackets `[]` indicate that the search yielded zero results for that specific term. **It's possible that:** 1. There are genuinely no such cases recorded under that precise label. 2. Cases that might be related to "thrift" (e.g., incidents at second-hand stores, charity shops, pawn shops) are categorized under different, more general terms (like "retail theft," "burglary - commercial," "fraud," or specific business names). Would you like me to try searching with alternative keywords, or do you have more specific details about what you're looking for?

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:14:32

Your AI is actually behaving correctly based on the SQL it generated. The issue is that the prompt interpreted **"thrift"** literally instead of understanding you meant **"theft"**.

It generated:

```sql
SELECT * FROM casemaster
WHERE crime_type = 'Thrift';
```

Your database contains:

```text
Theft
```

not

```text
Thrift
```

So it returned 0 rows.

---

## Fix 1 (Recommended): Improve the Gemini prompt

In your prompt (or system instructions), add guidance like this:

```text
You are an AI assistant for a crime investigation system.

Correct common spelling mistakes before generating SQL.

Examples:
- thrift -> theft
- thief -> theft
- robber -> robbery
- murder case -> Murder
- fir -> FIR

Always use the closest matching crime_type from the database schema.
```

---

## Fix 2: Use `ILIKE` instead of exact match

Instead of:

```sql
WHERE crime_type = 'Theft'
```

generate:

```sql
WHERE crime_type ILIKE '%theft%'
```

This is much more forgiving for capitalization and partial matches.

---

## Fix 3: Let the AI see valid crime types

Include the available values in the prompt:

```text
Valid crime types include:
- Theft
- Murder
- Robbery
- Assault
- Fraud
- Cyber Crime
```

Then Gemini is more likely to normalize "thrift" to "theft".

---

## Fix 4: Preprocess the user's question (optional)

Before sending the question to Gemini, correct common mistakes in Python:

```python
corrections = {
    "thrift": "theft",
    "theif": "theft",
    "murdur": "murder",
    "robery": "robbery",
}

question = question.lower()

for wrong, correct in corrections.items():
    question = question.replace(wrong, correct)
```

Then send the corrected question to Gemini.

---

### Expected result

If the user types:

```text
show all thrift cases
```

the AI should internally treat it as:

```text
show all theft cases
```

and generate:

```sql
SELECT *
FROM casemaster
WHERE crime_type ILIKE '%theft%';
```

which will correctly return your theft cases. This small improvement makes the AI much more natural and forgiving of user typos.

## Prompt:
09/07/2026, 12:16:46

how to fix

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:16:45

The best fix is to make **Gemini understand spelling mistakes** instead of relying on exact matches. Since you're already using Gemini to generate SQL, this is easy to implement.

## Option 1: Improve your prompt ⭐ (Recommended)

Open:

```text
backend/app/ai/prompt.py
```

Replace it with something like:

```python
SYSTEM_PROMPT = """
You are an expert SQL generator for a Crime Investigation System.

Rules:
1. Generate only PostgreSQL SELECT queries.
2. Never generate INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE, DROP, ALTER.
3. Use only the tables and columns from the provided schema.
4. Understand spelling mistakes and synonyms.

Examples:
- thrift -> theft
- theif -> theft
- steeling -> theft
- robbery -> robbery
- killing -> murder
- cyber attack -> cyber crime

Crime types in database:
- Theft
- Murder
- Robbery
- Assault
- Fraud
- Cyber Crime

Always generate flexible queries using ILIKE.

Example:

User:
Show all theft cases

SQL:
SELECT *
FROM casemaster
WHERE crime_type ILIKE '%theft%';
"""
```

---

## Option 2: Correct spelling before sending to Gemini ⭐⭐⭐

In your `ai_service.py`, before calling Gemini:

```python
question = question.lower()

corrections = {
    "thrift": "theft",
    "theif": "theft",
    "steeling": "theft",
    "murdur": "murder",
    "robery": "robbery",
    "cyberattack": "cyber crime",
}

for wrong, right in corrections.items():
    question = question.replace(wrong, right)
```

Now:

```
show all thrift cases
```

becomes

```
show all theft cases
```

before Gemini even sees it.

---

## Option 3: Make SQL more flexible

Instead of generating:

```sql
WHERE crime_type = 'Theft'
```

always generate:

```sql
WHERE crime_type ILIKE '%theft%'
```

This works even if the value is:

```
Theft
Vehicle Theft
Mobile Theft
Theft Case
```

---

## Option 4: Tell Gemini the database values

When building the prompt, include:

```
Available crime_type values:

Theft
Murder
Robbery
Fraud
Cyber Crime
Assault
```

Gemini is much better at mapping user input to known values when it knows the allowed options.

---

Use **all three**:

- ✅ Better prompt
- ✅ Python typo correction
- ✅ `ILIKE` instead of `=`

This combination gives the best user experience.

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:19:55

The error clearly tells you what's wrong:

```text
ImportError: cannot import name 'RULES' from 'app.ai.prompt'
```

Your file:

```python
app/ai/sql_generator.py
```

contains:

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
```

But in `app/ai/prompt.py`, there is **no variable named `RULES`**. You probably replaced it with something like:

```python
SYSTEM_PROMPT = """
...
"""
```

## Fix Option 1 (Recommended)

Open:

```text
app/ai/sql_generator.py
```

Change

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
```

to

```python
from app.ai.prompt import SYSTEM_PROMPT
```

Then, everywhere you use `RULES`, replace it with `SYSTEM_PROMPT`.

For example, if you have:

```python
prompt = f"""
{RULES}

Schema:
{schema}

Question:
{question}
"""
```

change it to:

```python
prompt = f"""
{SYSTEM_PROMPT}

Schema:
{schema}

Question:
{question}
"""
```

---

## Fix Option 2

If you want to keep the rest of your code unchanged, open:

```text
app/ai/prompt.py
```

and rename:

```python
SYSTEM_PROMPT = """
...
"""
```

to

```python
RULES = """
...
"""
```

That will satisfy:

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
```

---

- `SYSTEM_PROMPT`

instead of a generic `RULES`.

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
```

```python
from app.ai.prompt import SYSTEM_PROMPT
```

### If `prompt.py` is empty or broken, replace it with this:

```python
SYSTEM_PROMPT = """
You are an expert PostgreSQL SQL generator for a Crime Investigation System.

Rules:
- Generate ONLY SELECT statements.
- Never generate INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE, DROP, ALTER or TRUNCATE.
- Use only the tables and columns provided in the schema.
- Correct spelling mistakes automatically.
- Use ILIKE instead of = when searching text.
- Return ONLY SQL. No explanation. No markdown.

Examples:
User: Show all thrift cases
SQL:
```

```python
from app.ai.prompt import SYSTEM_PROMPT
```

## Response:
09/07/2026, 12:28:21

I found the bug. 🎯

Your `sql_generator.py` has two mistakes:

1. You're importing `RULES` twice.
2. You're calling `SYSTEM_PROMPT()` even though **it doesn't exist**. Your prompt file defines `RULES`, not `SYSTEM_PROMPT`.

Replace your entire `backend/app/ai/sql_generator.py` with this:

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
from app.ai.schema_loader import load_schema
from app.ai.gemini_client import ask_gemini

def generate_sql(question: str):
    schema = load_schema()

    prompt = f"""
{RULES}

Database Schema:

{schema}

User Question:

{question}

SQL:
"""

    return ask_gemini(prompt).strip()
```

### Remove these lines completely:

```python
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
from app.ai.prompt import RULES
```

(Keep only one import.)

And delete this incorrect line:

```python
schema = SYSTEM_PROMPT()
```

Replace it with:

```python
schema = load_schema()
```

---

After saving, restart the backend:

```bash
Ctrl + C
uvicorn app.main:app --reload
```

or whatever command you normally use.

### Expected result

You should see something like:

```
INFO: Uvicorn running on http://127.0.0.1:8000
Application startup complete.
```

with **no ImportError**.

After that, test:

```
Show all theft cases
```

If it starts successfully, we'll make the AI even smarter so it automatically understands typos like:

- `thrift` → `theft`
- `murdr` → `murder`
- `cyber fraud` → `Cyber Crime`

without needing explicit examples.

now to deploy this to zoho catalyst

## Response:
09/07/2026, 13:51:00

Since you're building **KPS Crime AI** with **React + FastAPI + PostgreSQL + Gemini**, here's the best way to deploy it on **Zoho Catalyst**.

> **Important:** Catalyst **does not support running FastAPI directly as a normal Python backend** the same way Render or Railway does. To deploy your existing project, you have two options.

---

# Option 1 (Recommended) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐

Deploy your existing project with only small changes.

```
React
        ↓
Catalyst AppSail
        ↓
FastAPI
        ↓
PostgreSQL
        ↓
Gemini API
```

AppSail can run Docker applications, which is ideal for your existing FastAPI backend.

---

# Project Structure

```
KPS-Crime-AI/

backend/
    app/
    requirements.txt
    Dockerfile

frontend/
    package.json
    vite.config.js

docker-compose.yml
```

---

# Step 1

Install Catalyst CLI

```
npm install -g zcatalyst-cli
```

Login

```
catalyst login
```

Create project

```
catalyst init
```

---

# Step 2

Create Dockerfile

Backend/Dockerfile

```dockerfile
FROM python:3.11

WORKDIR /app

COPY . .

RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

EXPOSE 8000

CMD ["uvicorn","app.main:app","--host","0.0.0.0","--port","8000"]
```

---

# Step 3

Create requirements.txt

```
fastapi
uvicorn
sqlalchemy
psycopg2-binary
python-dotenv
google-genai
pydantic
```

---

# Step 4

Frontend

```
npm run build
```

Produces

```
dist/
```

---

# Step 5

Deploy React

```
catalyst deploy
```

or

Upload

```
frontend/dist
```

as the web client.

---

# Step 6

Deploy Backend

```
catalyst appsail:add
```

Choose

```
Docker
```

Point to

```
backend/
```

Catalyst builds automatically.

---

# Step 7

Environment Variables

Add

```
DATABASE_URL=

GEMINI_API_KEY=

ALLOWED_ORIGINS=

PORT=8000
```

---

# Step 8

PostgreSQL

If using Catalyst Data Store:

```
SQLAlchemy

↓

Catalyst SDK

↓

Data Store
```

But **I recommend keeping PostgreSQL** (Neon, Supabase, Aiven, etc.) because your app already uses SQLAlchemy and joins extensively.

---

# Step 9

Update CORS

```python
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware

app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=[
        "https://yourfrontend.catalystapp.com"
    ],
    allow_credentials=True,
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"]
)
```

---

# Step 10

Deploy

```
catalyst deploy
```

---

# Final Architecture

```
React (Catalyst Hosting)

↓

FastAPI (AppSail)

↓

PostgreSQL

↓

Gemini API

↓

Crime AI
```

---

# Option 2 (Best for Hackathons) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐

If this project is for a hackathon, a more polished architecture is:

```
Catalyst Authentication

↓

React

↓

Catalyst Functions

↓

FastAPI AI Service

↓

PostgreSQL

↓

Gemini

↓

Catalyst File Store

↓

Catalyst Cache

↓

Catalyst Cron

↓

Catalyst Event Bus
```

This lets you showcase more Catalyst-native services while keeping your existing AI backend.

## My recommendation for your project

Because you've already built a working **React + FastAPI + PostgreSQL + Gemini** application, I recommend:

- ✅ React → Catalyst Web Hosting

This approach requires the fewest code changes while making full use of the Catalyst platform.

10/07/2026, 00:14:07

can i use live kit for voice conveztion in muilti language

## Response:
10/07/2026, 00:14:04

Yes. **LiveKit is one of the best choices** if you want a **real-time multilingual voice conversation** for your KSP Crime AI assistant. 🚀

For your project, I'd recommend this architecture:

```
Officer
   │
🎤 Voice
   │
LiveKit Voice Agent
   │
Speech-to-Text (Deepgram / AssemblyAI / Google)
   │
LLM (Gemini 2.5 / GPT-5)
   │
FastAPI
   │
PostgreSQL Crime Database
   │
AI Response
   │
Text-to-Speech (ElevenLabs / Cartesia / Google TTS)
   │
🔊 LiveKit streams audio back
```

### What LiveKit provides
- ✅ Real-time voice conversations (low latency)
- ✅ Audio streaming
- ✅ WebRTC infrastructure
- ✅ Interruptions ("barge-in" while AI is speaking)
- ✅ Echo cancellation
- ✅ Noise suppression
- ✅ Speaker detection
- ✅ Browser, Android, and iOS support

### Multilingual support
LiveKit itself doesn't translate languages—it streams audio. The multilingual capability comes from the speech and AI models you connect to it.

For Indian police use:

| Feature | Recommended |
|---------|-------------|
| Speech-to-Text | Deepgram Nova-3 |
| LLM | Gemini 2.5 Flash / GPT-5 |
| Translation | Gemini 2.5 (built-in multilingual) |
| Text-to-Speech | ElevenLabs Multilingual v2 |

This supports conversations such as:
- 🇮🇳 English
- 🇮🇳 Kannada
- 🇮🇳 Hindi
- 🇮🇳 Tamil
- 🇮🇳 Telugu
- 🇮🇳 Malayalam

For example:

Officer:
> "ಬೆಂಗಳೂರುದಲ್ಲಿ ಕಳೆದ ತಿಂಗಳ ಕಳ್ಳತನ ಪ್ರಕರಣಗಳನ್ನು ತೋರಿಸಿ."

↓

Gemini understands Kannada.

↓

Generates SQL:

```sql
SELECT *
FROM casemaster
WHERE district='Bengaluru'
AND crime_type ILIKE '%Theft%';
```

↓

AI replies in Kannada.

↓

LiveKit streams the spoken Kannada response.

### Features you can build
- 🎤 Push-to-talk
- 🎙️ Continuous conversation
- 🌐 Automatic language detection
- 🔄 Switch language mid-conversation
- 🗣️ Natural voice responses
- 👮 Officer authentication
- 📄 Read FIR summaries aloud
- 🚓 Hands-free use in patrol vehicles

### Cost
- LiveKit Cloud has a free tier suitable for development.
- You can also self-host LiveKit if you want more control.

### For your KSP Crime AI
Based on your current stack (React + FastAPI + PostgreSQL + Gemini), I recommend:

- **Frontend:** React
- **Voice transport:** LiveKit
- **Speech-to-Text:** Deepgram Nova-3
- **LLM:** Gemini 2.5 Flash
- **Backend:** FastAPI
- **Database:** PostgreSQL
- **Text-to-Speech:** ElevenLabs Multilingual v2

This combination gives you a fast, multilingual, natural voice assistant that fits well with your existing architecture and hackathon goals.
